<h1 align="center" style="font-weight:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;page-break-after:auto;text-align:center;text-decoration:underline;text-indent:-.5in;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Kraft Foods Inc.
Reports Second Quarter 2004 Results</font></u></b></h1>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">&#149;</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i><font style="font-style:italic;">Net Revenues Up 4.6% On
Volume Growth Of 3.6%</font></i></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">&#149;</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i><font style="font-style:italic;">Diluted E.P.S. Of $0.41 (Including $0.05 In Asset Impairment, Exit And Implementation Costs For The
Restructuring Program) Down 25.5% Versus 2003</font></i></p>

<p align="left" style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">&#149;</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i><font style="font-style:italic;">Cost Restructuring Program On
Track To Deliver Targeted Savings</font></i></p>

<p align="left" style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">&#149;</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i><font style="font-style:italic;">2004 Full Year E.P.S. Guidance Revised to $1.55-$1.62
(Including $0.30 In Exit And Implementation Costs For
The Restructuring Program And Asset Impairment Charges) Due Primarily To Higher
Commodity Costs, Particularly Dairy</font></i></p>

<p style="line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">NORTHFIELD, IL &#150; July 19,
2004 &#150; Kraft Foods Inc. (NYSE: KFT) today reported second quarter 2004 results
and progress against its Sustainable Growth Plan.&#160; Net revenues were up 4.6% driven by currency,
tack-on acquisitions, new products and the impact of increased marketing
spending.&#160; Diluted earnings per share of
$0.41 were down 25.5% versus 2003, reflecting increased commodity costs, higher
marketing spending, and asset impairment and exit costs for the restructuring
program announced in January, partially offset by the impact of pricing
actions.&#160; The company revised its 2004
full year earnings per share guidance range to $1.55-$1.62 (including an
estimated $0.30 per share in asset impairment, exit and implementation costs
for the restructuring program), which is in line with current Street estimates,
due primarily to higher commodity costs, particularly dairy.&#160; At the end of the second quarter, dairy costs
moderated from the record highs reached in April.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#147;Kraft&#146;s
second quarter results reflect continued progress against the company&#146;s
Sustainable Growth Plan.&#160; In North
America, consumption and market share trends improved more broadly across our
portfolio behind increased marketing spending, and we are successfully
integrating the Veryfine acquisition.&#160; Additionally, we are on track to deliver the
targeted cost savings from our restructuring program,&#148; said Roger Deromedi, Chief Executive Officer of Kraft Foods. &#147;However,
volume in our International business was softer than expected due to increased
price competition in a few key markets.&#148;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Deromedi</font>
added, &#147;Significantly higher costs for our key commodities, especially dairy,
drove both the earnings decline in the quarter and the need to revise our 2004
full year earnings guidance.&#160; As I indicated
in January, the highest priority of our Sustainable Growth Plan is to reinvest
in our brands, including the management of price gaps in certain businesses,
and we have made good progress against this
priority.&#160; We remain committed to
improving the long-term health of our brands, and will not let short-term</p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">1</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>


<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='',FILE='C:\JMS\lsmith\04-7910-1\task148807\7910-1-mm.htm',USER='lsmith',CD='Jul 18 15:24 2004' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">commodity</font>
market fluctuations distract us from this key imperative.&#160; With the recent decline in cheese costs in
the last several weeks to more historical levels, we believe our strategy of
increasing prices based on our full year outlook versus the short-term second
quarter spike was not only consistent with our Sustainable Growth Plan, but
also positioned us well for the back half of 2004.&#148;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<h6 align="center" style="line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;page-break-after:auto;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;text-decoration:underline;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Second
Quarter Results</font></u></b></h6>

<p align="left" style="line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-align:left;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Second
quarter diluted earnings per share were down 25.5% ($0.14 per share) versus the
prior year due primarily to a decline in operating income of 23.7%.&#160; Earnings per share were impacted by higher
commodity costs ($0.10 per share), increased marketing investment ($0.06 per
share), asset impairment, exit and implementation costs for the restructuring
program ($0.05 per share) and increased benefit costs and restricted stock
expense ($0.02 per share), partially offset by restructuring savings ($0.01 per
share), favorable currency ($0.01 per share) and all other operations ($0.07
per share).</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Costs for
several commodities were up in the quarter, with the most significant increase
in dairy costs.&#160; Second quarter average
cost for U.S. barrel cheese was up 70% versus the second quarter of last year
and up 53% versus the five-year average, resulting in increased costs of
approximately $200 million versus prior year (after-tax equivalent of
approximately $0.08 per share).&#160; In
response to the higher costs, the company increased prices on its different
varieties of U.S. cheeses by 5%-15%.&#160;
However, the pricing actions were not designed to fully offset the
higher costs because of the company&#146;s expectation that cheese costs would not
remain at historical highs.&#160; On the
quarter, the price increases offset approximately one-half of the higher costs.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Net revenues
increased $364 million, or 4.6%, due to favorable currency of $237 million (3.0
pts.), volume/mix (0.8 pts.) and net pricing (0.6 pts.).&#160; Total reported volume was up 3.6% as ongoing
volume growth of 3.9% (including 3.1 pts. of growth from acquisitions) was
slightly offset by the impact of divestitures.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kraft North
America Commercial (KNAC) ongoing volume was up 4.9% (including 3.8 pts. from
acquisitions) as strong growth in categories with increased marketing was
partially offset by significant declines in cereal and confections, which were
impacted by competitive activity, low carbohydrate diet trends and the timing
of new product introductions versus last year.&#160;
Kraft International Commercial (KIC) ongoing volume was up 1.1%, with
1.3 percentage points coming from acquisitions.&#160;
Developing markets grew solidly, despite a double-digit decline in
beverages in Mexico due to increased price competition from the carbonated
beverage segment.&#160; This growth was
partially offset by softness in Western Europe, particularly France, due to
price competition.&#160; New product innovations
progressed on track in the quarter, including solid results for several biscuit
items in North America.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">2</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As part of the company&#146;s
plan to reinvest in its brands, in-market spending was up approximately $170
million in the quarter.&#160; Approximately
80% of the increase was in North America, where businesses that increased
marketing spending by at least 10% &#151; cheese, coffee, lunch combinations, meat,
salad dressing, snack nuts, Foodservice and Canadian retail &#151; in aggregate
delivered net revenue growth of 7% and volume growth of 4%.&#160; In the company&#146;s top 25 North American
categories (based on operating companies income, or OCI), market share was up
in categories representing 51% of OCI, reflecting sequential improvement from
both full year 2003 (38% of OCI) and first quarter 2004 (39% of OCI) results.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The previously
announced restructuring program progressed on track in the quarter.&#160; The company announced the exit or closure of
seven additional plants (12 plants year-to-date) and elimination of over 700
positions worldwide (over 2,600 positions year-to-date).&#160; Second quarter pre-tax charges and savings
from the program were $138 million and $31 million, respectively.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On April 7,
2004, the company announced an agreement with Tazo
Tea Company, a wholly owned subsidiary of Starbucks Corporation, to license the
<b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Tazo</font></b>
line of tea products, including hot tea and bottled ready-to-drink iced and
juice-flavored teas, for sale in retail grocery, club, convenience,
mass merchant and natural channels across the United States.&#160; Additionally, on June 9, 2004, the company
announced an alliance with Dr. Arthur Agatston,
cardiologist and creator of the South Beach Diet, to use the <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">South Beach Diet</font></b> trademark to promote
certain Kraft products.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Discretionary
cash flow (net cash provided by operating activities less capital expenditures)
declined $103 million to $979 million through the first half of 2004, due
primarily to voluntary contributions to the company&#146;s pension plans of $320
million and lower earnings, partially offset by lower capital spending.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">During the
quarter, the company declared a regular quarterly dividend of $0.18 per common
share and repurchased 5.2 million shares of Class A common stock for $162
million.&#160; To date, the company has spent
$375 million (including $50 million in December 2003) to purchase 11.7 million
shares under a two-year, $700 million stock repurchase program authorized in
December 2003.&#160; The company expects to
complete the $700 million program by the end of 2004.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<h4 align="center" style="line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt 2.9pt;page-break-after:auto;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;text-decoration:underline;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">2004
Outlook</font></u></b></h4>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The company
updated its full year 2004 diluted earnings per share guidance range to
$1.55-$1.62, including an estimated $0.30 per share impact from asset
impairment charges, exit and implementation costs for the restructuring
program.&#160; This range is below the
company&#146;s original January 2004 guidance, due primarily to higher commodity
costs that the company does not expect to fully recover through pricing actions
in 2004 (approximately $0.11 per share), partially offset by a lower than
expected tax rate of 33% (approximately $0.03 per share).&#160; Additionally, the current guidance reflects
the impact of first half volume softness in Kraft International Commercial,
which was offset by favorable currency.&#160;
The current guidance</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">3</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">is</font>
slightly below the update given on April 19, 2004, which was the low end of the
original range, due to the sustained high dairy costs throughout the second
quarter and softer than expected International results.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The company
expects to incur $650-$700 million in higher commodity costs on the year, due
primarily to higher dairy costs, which will be only partially offset by pricing
and trade spending adjustments.&#160; The
company continues to project increased investment in consumer marketing and
price gap management of $500-$600 million versus 2003.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For the full
year, the company projects pre-tax asset impairment, exit and implementation
costs of $750-$800 million (after-tax equivalent of approximately $0.30 per
share) and pre-tax savings of $120-$140 million for the restructuring program.&#160; These projections are consistent with
previous guidance.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The company
maintained its guidance for full year constant currency net revenue growth
excluding divestitures(1) of around 3%, while
increasing its volume growth to around 3.5%.&#160;
The increase in full year volume expectations is due to the Veryfine acquisition, which adds approximately 2.0
percentage points to full year volume growth, while adding 0.5 percentage
points to full year revenue growth.&#160; The
revenue guidance reflects accelerated second half revenue growth versus the
first half due to the timing of new product launches, momentum behind the
increased marketing spending, the impact of pricing actions, and the lapping of
the impact of the European heat wave in the prior year.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The company
projects full year 2004 discretionary cash flow of $2.6 billion.&#160; The change versus previous guidance reflects
the reduction in earnings guidance and voluntary contributions to pension
plans, partially offset by lower capital spending and working capital improvements.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">As described in &#147;Note 13, Segment Reporting&#148; of Kraft Foods Inc.&#146;s 2003
Annual Report, management reviews operating companies income (OCI), which is
defined as operating income before corporate expenses and amortization of
intangibles, to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources.&#160; Management believes it is appropriate to
disclose this measure to help investors analyze business performance and
trends.&#160; (For a reconciliation of OCI to
operating income, see the Condensed Statements of Earnings contained in this
release.)</font></i></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></i></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">The source of market share data included in the Kraft North America
Commercial section below is A.C. Nielsen (3-outlet data, excluding Wal-Mart).</font></i></p>

guidance on a constant currency basis excluding divestitures and including
acquisitions because it believes this measure provides better year-to-year
comparability of results.&#160; Additionally,
the company is unable to predict future movements of foreign exchange rates and
the exact timing and nature of future divestitures.&#160; Each of these factors could result in a
significant difference in revenue results.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;page-break-after:auto;text-align:center;text-autospace:ideograph-numeric ideograph-other;text-decoration:underline;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kraft
North America Commercial</font></u></b></p>

<p align="left" style="line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Operating companies
income declined 20.7% to $1,063 million due to higher commodity costs net of
pricing, increased marketing investment, higher benefit costs and exit and
implementation costs for the restructuring program of $48 million, partially
offset by the contribution from volume growth and favorable currency.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Net revenues
grew 3.7% to $5,697 million as higher volumes including acquisitions;
commodity-driven pricing on cheese, meats and foodservice; and favorable
currency of $40 million were partially offset by increased promotional
spending.&#160; Volume was up 4.9% (including
3.8 pts. of growth from acquisitions) behind solid growth in categories with
increased marketing spending as part of the Sustainable Growth Plan, including
cheese, coffee, cold cuts and salted snacks.&#160;
These gains were partially offset by declines in categories facing
challenges from the low carbohydrate diet trends, including cereals and
confections.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Following are second quarter results by segment for KNAC:</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></i></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">U.S. Beverages and Grocery</font></u></i>
net revenues increased 0.8% as volume growth of 10.2%, driven by the Veryfineacquisition
(8.5 pts.), was largely offset by adverse product mix and higher promotional
spending.&#160; Mid single-digit volume growth
in Beverages (excluding the Veryfine acquisition) and
Coffee was partially offset by a significant decline in Cereals volume.&#160; Beverage volume growth was driven by the
introduction of <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Capri Sun</font></b> Fruit Waves beverages and growth in non-measured channels.&#160; Coffee volume and share were both up driven
by increased marketing spending, including <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Maxwell
House</font></b> coffee advertising that communicates recent product quality
improvements.&#160; Enhancers
volume was up reflecting growth in <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Kraft</font></b>
mayonnaise and barbecue sauce, particularly in non-measured channels.&#160; The significant Cereals decline was
attributable to competitive new products and spending and the low carbohydrate
diet trend impact on the category.&#160;
Segment OCI decreased 13.5% to $473 million due to increased marketing
investment and higher commodity and benefit costs, partially offset by the
contribution from higher volume.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></i></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">U.S. Snacks</font></u></i> net
revenues were down 1.4% due to essentially flat volume and adverse product mix&#160; (growth in Salted
Snacks offset by a decline in Confections).&#160;
Biscuit shipments were flat versus prior year, reflecting the positive
impact of business growth initiatives offset by weak category trends due to low
carbohydrate diet trends.&#160; Cookie share
was up 0.7 points in the quarter reflecting the impact of recently introduced
Golden <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Oreo, Chips Ahoy</font></b> Chunky
White Fudge and <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Snackwell&#146;s</font></b><b><font style="font-weight:bold;"> CarbWell</font></b>
cookies.&#160; In crackers, continued momentum
in <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Ritz </font></b>Chips was offset by
increased competition in the cheese cracker segment.&#160; Snack Nuts continued to deliver double-digit
volume gains aided by increased marketing spending on the <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Planters </font></b>brand and increased consumer
awareness of the nutritional benefits of nuts.&#160;
Confections volume was down double-digits due to category softness, the
timing of new product</p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">5</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">introductions</font>
versus prior year, and increased competition in fruit snacks.&#160; Segment OCI declined 27.4% to $183 million
due to increased marketing investment, higher commodity and benefit costs,
adverse product mix and exit and implementation costs for the restructuring
program of $17 million, partially offset by the absence of high product returns
associated with new products incurred in the prior year.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></i></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">U.S. Cheese, Canada &amp; North America
Foodservice</font></u></i> net revenues were up 10.0% on volume
growth of 3.2% (including 1.6 pts. from acquisitions), commodity-driven pricing
in Cheese and Foodservice and favorable currency of $40 million, partially
offset by higher promotional reinvestment spending in Cheese.&#160; Cheese posted a strong quarter with increased
overall volume, and share gains in all key segments, including Process Slices
(+3.4 pts.), Naturals (+2.5 pts.) and Cream Cheese (+2.5 pts.).&#160; Canada volume was up, reflecting growth in
beverages behind the launches of <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Kool-Aid</font></b>
Sport and new <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Kool-Aid</font></b>  Jammers flavors, while North America Foodservice volume
grew due to strength in national accounts.&#160;
Segment OCI declined 35.7% to $220 million due to higher commodity costs
net of pricing, increased marketing investment, higher benefit costs and exit
and implementation costs for the restructuring program of $28 million,
partially offset by volume growth and favorable currency of $7 million.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></i></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">U.S. Convenient Meals</font></u></i>
net revenues increased 3.8% due to commodity-driven price increases in meats
and pizza and a slight volume increase (up 0.2%).&#160; <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Oscar Mayer</font></b>
volume growth was driven by solid consumption gains in cold cuts and hot dogs
behind increased marketing spending.&#160;
Excluding the exit of certain product lines last year, Meals volume was
flat versus prior year.&#160; Pizza volume was
down modestly, reflecting a challenging competitive environment, although
consumption showed solid improvement in the final month of the quarter due to
the launch of <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">DiGiorno</font></b>
Thin Crispy Crust Pizza.&#160; Segment OCI
declined 6.0% to $187 million due to higher commodity costs net of pricing and
higher benefit costs, partially offset by favorable product mix.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;page-break-after:auto;text-align:center;text-autospace:ideograph-numeric ideograph-other;text-decoration:underline;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kraft
International Commercial</font></u></b></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">Operating companies income decreased 33.6% to $225 million, as exit
costs for the restructuring program of $90 million, higher marketing
investment, increased product costs, unfavorable mix and the impact of
divestitures were partially offset by favorable currency of $19 million.</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">Net revenues grew
6.8% to $2,508 million, as favorable currency of $197 million and volume gains
from acquisitions were partially offset by the impact of divestitures and
increased promotional spending in Europe.&#160;
Volume was down 0.2% due to divestitures, while volume from ongoing
businesses was up 1.1%, benefiting from tack-on acquisitions, which accounted
for 1.3 percentage points of growth. Overall developing market growth was
solid, driven by gains in Argentina, Brazil, China and Puerto Rico, despite a
double-digit decline in beverages in Mexico and weakness in Russia.&#160; Developing market</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">6</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>


<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='',FILE='C:\JMS\lsmith\04-7910-1\task148807\7910-1-mm.htm',USER='lsmith',CD='Jul 18 15:24 2004' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:0in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">growth</font><font color="black" style="color:windowtext;"> was offset by lower volume in
portions of Western Europe, including France, due to price competition and
discount trade dynamics, and the Nordic region impacted by the transportation
strike in Norway.</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">Following are second
quarter results by segment for KIC:</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></i></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Europe, Middle East &amp; Africa (EMEA)</font></u></i> net revenues increased 8.0% as favorable
currency of $169 million and volume gains from acquisitions were partially
offset by the impact of divestitures and reduced prices due to increased
competition.&#160; Volume was down 0.8%, with
offsetting impacts from last year&#146;s acquisition of Family Nutrition in Egypt
(2.3 pts.) and divestitures of a rice business in Germany and a cheese business
in Italy (2.2 pts.).&#160; Segment OCI
decreased 38.4% to $143 million, reflecting exit costs for the restructuring
program of $81 million, lower pricing, higher marketing investment and the
impact of divestitures, partially offset by favorable currency of $20 million.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">EMEA beverages volume decreased due to coffee, which was impacted by market
softness and price competition, particularly in France.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">EMEA snacks volume increased, driven by biscuits, due to acquisitions,
partially offset by a decline in confectionery, reflecting price competition
and trade inventory reductions in Russia and a national transportation strike
in Norway. In Germany, volume grew strongly, driven by the launch of <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Milka</font></b><b><font style="font-weight:bold;"> M-joy</font></b>
chocolate tablets, while in Benelux, confectionery volume was up due to more impactful promotions in the Netherlands.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">EMEA cheese volume was lower, impacted by the divestiture of the <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Invernizzi</font></b> business in
Europe. Ongoing cheese volume grew, with gains in <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Philadelphia</font></b>
cream cheese across most markets, including the impact of new product launches
in Italy and successful promotions in Germany.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">EMEA grocery volume increased primarily due to the acquisition in
Egypt, while EMEA convenient meals volume decreased, impacted by the
divestiture of the <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">r</font></b><b><font style="font-weight:bold;">eis</font></b><b><font style="font-weight:bold;">-fit</font></b> business
in Europe.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></i></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Latin America &amp; Asia Pacific (LAAP)</font></u></i>
net revenues increased 3.8% driven by favorable currency and pricing actions,
partially offset by adverse mix and higher promotional spending.&#160; Volume was up 0.7%, with growth in both the
Latin America and Asia Pacific regions.&#160;
Segment OCI decreased 23.4% to $82 million, as exit costs for the
restructuring program of $9 million, adverse mix, higher marketing investment
and product costs were partially offset by price increases.</p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5pt;text-indent:.05pt;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">LAAP snacks volume was flat to prior year, as
growth in confectionery in Argentina and Brazil was offset by a decline in
biscuits in Venezuela and Southeast Asia.</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .55pt;text-indent:.05pt;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">LAAP beverages volume decreased as a
double-digit decline in Mexico, impacted by price competition from the
carbonated beverage segment, was moderated by growth in Puerto Rico, Brazil and
China.&#160; LAAP cheese volume growth was
strong, with gains across all key markets, including Australia and the
Philippines.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">*&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;
*&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; *</font></p>

<p style="line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">7</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
company will host a conference call for members of the investment community to
review its second quarter results from 12:00-1:00 p.m. ET on July 19,
2004.&#160; Additionally, the company will webcast management presentations and question and answer
sessions on the progress it has made toward its Sustainable Growth Plan
beginning at 2:00 p.m. ET.&#160; Access to a
live audio webcast is available at www.kraft.com and
a replay of the conference call and webcast
presentations will be available on the company&#146;s web site.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kraft Foods Inc. is the largest branded food and beverage company
headquartered in the United States and the second largest worldwide.&#160; Kraft Foods markets many of the world&#146;s
leading food brands, including <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Kraft</font></b> cheese, <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Jacobs</font></b> and <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Maxwell House</font></b>
coffees, <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Nabisco</font></b> cookies and crackers, <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Philadelphia </font></b>cream cheese, <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Oscar Mayer</font></b>
meats, <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Post</font></b> cereals and <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Milka</font></b> chocolates, in more than 150 countries.</font></p>

<h3 align="center" style="line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;page-break-after:auto;text-align:center;text-transform:uppercase;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></b></h3>

<h3 align="center" style="line-height:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;page-break-after:auto;text-align:center;text-transform:uppercase;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;text-transform:none;">Forward-Looking
and Cautionary Statements</font></u></b></h3>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">This press
release contains projections of future results and other forward-looking

1995, the company is hereby identifying important factors that could cause

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Each of the company&#146;s
segments is subject to intense competition, changes in consumer preferences and
demand for its products, including low carbohydrate
diet trends, the effects of changing prices for its raw materials and local
economic and market conditions. Their results are dependent upon their
continued ability to promote brand equity successfully, to anticipate and
respond to new consumer trends, to develop new products and markets, to broaden
brand portfolios, to compete effectively with lower priced products in a
consolidating environment at the retail and manufacturing levels and to improve
productivity. The company&#146;s results are also dependent on its ability to
consummate and successfully integrate acquisitions and to realize the cost
savings and improved asset utilization contemplated by its restructuring
program. In addition, the company is subject to the effects of foreign
economies, currency movements, fluctuations in</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

competitive environment. The company&#146;s results are affected by its access to
credit markets, borrowing costs and credit ratings, which may in turn be
influenced by the credit ratings of Altria
Group,&nbsp;Inc. The company&#146;s benefit expense is subject to the investment
performance of pension plan assets, interest rates and cost increases for
medical benefits offered to employees and retirees. The company&#146;s assessment of the fair value of
its operations for purposes of assessing impairment of goodwill and intangibles
is based on discounting projections of future cash flows and is affected by the
interest rate market and general economic and market conditions. The food industry continues to be subject to
recalls if products become adulterated or misbranded, liability if product
consumption causes injury, ingredient disclosure and labeling laws and
regulations and the possibility that consumers could lose confidence in the
safety and quality of certain food products. The food industry is also subject
to consumer concerns regarding genetically modified organisms and the health
implications of obesity and trans-fatty acids. Developments in any of these
areas could cause the company&#146;s results to differ materially from results that
have been or may be projected by or on behalf of the company. The company
cautions that the foregoing list of important factors is not exclusive. Any forward-looking
statements in this press release are made as of the date hereof. The company
does not undertake to update any forward-looking statement.</p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">KRAFT FOODS INC.</font></b></p>

<p align="center" style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">and</font> Subsidiaries</p>
